Moreover, determining whether similar mechanisms exist that induce or offset the loss of the TIR domain in both eudicots and monocots will be of great interest.</p><p>Although many studies have focused on the mechanisms of lipid biosynthesis and accumulation and the detection of lipid-related genes in different species, the genes involved in the dozens of complex oil biosynthesis pathways require further elucidation. For primary edible oil crops such as rapeseed, peanut and soybean, it is inextricable to encounter intertwined polyploidy or large genome sizes with many lipid-relates genes, which makes studies on oil biosynthesis much more daunting. In contrast, the higher oil content and fewer lipid-related genes in the small and diploid genome of sesame make it an invaluable potential model plant for studying oil biosynthesis. The <i>de novo</i> assembled genome, a set of 12 transcriptomes and 29 resequenced accessions provide a large resource for exploring the mechanisms underlying different oil content between sesame and soybean, as well as among sesame accessions. The extensive expansion and high diversity of LTP1 genes, and key genes differentially expressed in downstream of the TAG biosynthesis pathway should aid future genetic studies in sesame. Undoubtedly, future studies on sesame will help to improve the quantity and quality of edible oil crops in order to fight food and nutrition crises.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec15" data-title="Materials and methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec15-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec15">Materials and methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec15-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">DNA and RNA isolation</h3><p>The genotype used for whole genome <i>de novo</i> sequencing was Zhongzhi No. 13, an elite sesame cultivar that has been introduced to most of the major sesame planting areas over the past 10 years. Genomic DNA was extracted from leaves with a standard CTAB (Cetyl trimethylammonium bromide) extraction method [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Doyle JJ, Doyle JL: Isolation of plant DNA from fresh tissue. Focus. 1990, 12: 13-15." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2269">51</a>]. The materials used for RNA-Seq to analyze lipid and sesamin synthesis were three sesame accessions with different lipid and sesamin content (Table S1 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>). The seeds of 10, 20, 25 and 30 DPA plants were sampled for RNA-Seq. The procedure described by Wei <i>et al</i>. [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Wei W, Qi X, Wang L, Zhang Y, Hua W, Li D, Lv H, Zhang X: Characterization of the sesame (Sesamum indicum L.) global transcriptome using Illumina paired-end sequencing and development of EST-SSR markers. BMC Genomics. 2011, 12: 451-" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2278">17</a>] was used for RNA extraction and sequencing (or see Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">Whole genome shotgun sequencing and assembly</h3><p>We carried out whole genome shotgun sequencing with the Illumina Hiseq 2000 platform. Eight paired-end sequencing libraries with insert sizes of approximately 180 bp, 500 bp, 800 bp, 2 kb, 5 kb, 10 kb and 20 kb were constructed, which generated a total data amount of 99.54 Gb. To reduce the effect of sequencing error on assembly, we applied a series of stringent filtering steps on read generation (see Supplementary Note in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>). After the above quality-control and filtering steps, 54.46 Gb of clean data, approximately 150-fold coverage of the predicted genome size, remained (Table S2 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>; Data S1 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM2">2</a>). The quality and quantity of the filtered data were checked by the distributions of the clean reads from every library (Figure S1 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>). For all of the 37.63 Gb of clean data from short-insert size libraries, a custom program based on the <i>k-</i>mer frequency methodology was used to trim reads and correct bases [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="The Tomato Genome Consortium: The tomato genome sequence provides insights into fleshy fruit evolution. Nature. 2012, 485: 635-641." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2309">26</a>]. Next, all of the remaining data were used for <i>de novo</i> genome assembly. We carried out the whole genome assembly using SOAPdenovo [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Wang X, Wang H, Wang J, Sun R, Wu J, Liu S, Bai Y, Mun JH, Bancroft I, Cheng F, Huang S, Li X, Hua W, Wang J, Wang X, Freeling M, Pires JC, Paterson AH, Chalhoub B, Wang B, Hayward A, Sharpe AG, Park BS, Weisshaar B, Liu B, Li B, Liu B, Tong C, Song C, Duran C, et al: The genome of the mesopolyploid crop species Brassica rapa. Nat Genet. 2011, 43: 1035-1039." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2315">30</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Li R, Zhu H, Ruan J, Qian W, Fang X, Shi Z, Li Y, Li S, Shan G, Kristiansen K, Yang H, Wang J: De novo assembly of human genomes with massively parallel short read sequencing. Genome Res. 2010, 20: 265-272." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2318">52</a>].</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec18">Contig construction</h4><p>First, we split the reads from the short-insert size libraries into <i>k-</i>mers (k=71) and constructed a <i>de Bruijn</i> graph. We then simplified the graph referring to the parameters, and lastly connected the <i>k-</i>mer path to produce the contig file.</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec19">Scaffold construction</h4><p>All usable reads were realigned onto the contig sequences; the amount of shared paired end relationships between each pair of contigs and the rate of consistent and conflicting paired-ends were calculated to construct the scaffolds step by step, from short-insertion-size paired ends to long-insertion-size paired ends, and finally, scaffolds.</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec20">Gap filling</h4><p>We used the tool GapCloser [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="SOAPdenovo2: large-size Genome De-novo Assembler. &#xA;                    http://sourceforge.net/projects/soapdenovo2/files/GapCloser/&#xA;                    &#xA;                  ," href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2352">53</a>] to close the gaps inside the constructed scaffolds, which were mainly composed of repeats masked before scaffold construction. We used the paired-end information to retrieve the read pairs that had one end mapped to the unique contig and the other located in the gap region. Then, we preformed local assembly for these collected reads. Finally, about 274 Mb of the sesame genome was assembled, 98.8% of which is non-gapped sequences (Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Estimation of genome size by flow cytometry</h3><p>Flow cytometry was used to determine the DNA content of sesame [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Dolezel J, Greilhuber J, Suda J: Estimation of nuclear DNA content in plants using flow cytometry. Nat Protocols. 2007, 2: 2233-2244." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2367">54</a>]. Sesame samples and reference material were analyzed on an EPICS Elite ESP cytometer (Beckman-Coulter, Hialeah, FL, USA) with an air-cooled argon laser (Uniphase) at 488 nm using 20 mW. Salmon erythrocytes (2.16 pg/1C) were used as internal biological reference materials. Nuclear DNA content (in picograms) of sesame samples was estimated according to the following equation: 1C nuclear DNA content=(1C reference in picogramsPeak mean of sesame)/(Peak mean of reference). The number of base pairs per haploid genome was calculated based on the equivalent of 1 pg DNA=978 Mb [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Dolezel J, Bartos J, Voglmayr H, Greilhuber J: Nuclear DNA content and genome size of trout and human. Cytometry A. 2003, 51: 127-128. author reply 129" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2370">55</a>]. As a result, the C-value of sesame was estimated to be 0.34 pg/1C, and its genome size was estimated to be approximately 337 Mb (Figure S3 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">Anchoring of genome assembly to sesame genetic map</h3><p>We used a combination method of specific length amplified fragment sequencing and experiment marker analysis to construct a new genetic map using 107 F<sub>2</sub> lines derived from the Zhongzhi No.13/ZZM2289 population. In total, 2,719 SNPs, 97 insertions and deletions (indels) and 2,282 SSR markers were developed and screened against the population. After filtering the markers with low PCR quality, those having no polymorphism and those showing significantly distorted segregation in the population, the retained 45 indels, 259 SNPs and 124 SSR markers were used to construct the genetic map using JoinMap 3 software (Kyazma BV, Wageningen, Netherlands). Finally, we successfully constructed a genetic map that spans 1790.08 cM and has 406 markers, including 39 indels, 251 SNPs and 116 SSR markers. Based on the genetic map, 150 large scaffolds were anchored onto 16 pseudomolecules (see details in the Supplementary Note 3 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec23">Gene structure prediction and function annotation</h3><p>To predict genes in the assembled genome, we used both homology-based and <i>de novo</i> methods. For the homology-based prediction, <i>A. thaliana</i>, grapevine, castor, and potato proteins were mapped onto the assembled genome using Genewise [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Birney E, Durbin R: Using GeneWise in the Drosophila annotation experiment. Genome Res. 2000, 10: 547-548." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2404">56</a>] to define gene models. For <i>de novo</i> prediction, Augustus [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Stanke M, Keller O, Gunduz I, Hayes A, Waack S, Morgenstern B: AUGUSTUS: ab initio prediction of alternative transcripts. Nucleic Acids Res. 2006, 34: W435-W439." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2410">57</a>] and GlimmerHMM were employed using appropriate parameters. Data from these complementary analyses were merged to produce a non-redundant reference gene set using GLEAN [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="GLEAN. &#xA;                    http://glean-gene.sourceforge.net/&#xA;                    &#xA;                  ," href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2414">58</a>]. In addition, RNA-Seq data from multiple tissues (young roots, leaves, flowers, developing seeds, and shoot tips) from our previous study [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Wei W, Qi X, Wang L, Zhang Y, Hua W, Li D, Lv H, Zhang X: Characterization of the sesame (Sesamum indicum L.) global transcriptome using Illumina paired-end sequencing and development of EST-SSR markers. BMC Genomics. 2011, 12: 451-" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2417">17</a>] were also incorporated to aid in gene annotation. RNA-Seq data were mapped to the assembled genome using TopHat [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Trapnell C, Pachter L, Salzberg SL: TopHat: discovering splice junctions with RNA-Seq. Bioinformatics. 2009, 25: 1105-1111." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2420">59</a>], and transcriptome-based gene structures were obtained by cufflinks [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Cufflinks. &#xA;                    http://cufflinks.cbcb.umd.edu/&#xA;                    &#xA;                  ," href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2423">60</a>]. Then, we compared this gene set with the previous one to get the final non-redundant gene set of sesame (Tables S8 to S10 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>). The non-coding gene predictions and gene function annotations were conducted as described in Supplementary Note 3 and Table S11 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec24">Repeat annotation</h3><p>We identified repeat content in the sesame genome using a combination of <i>de novo</i> and homology-based approaches (Supplementary Note and Tables S12 and S13 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>). Full-length LTR retrotransposons were identified by LTR_STRUC [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="McCarthy EM, McDonald JF: LTR_STRUC: a novel search and identification program for LTR retrotransposons. Bioinformatics. 2003, 19: 362-367." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2446">61</a>] and classified as <i>Gypsy</i>, <i>Copia</i> and other types of transposons using the program RepeatClassifer implemented in the RepeatModeler package [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="RepeatMasker. &#xA;                    http://www.repeatmasker.org&#xA;                    &#xA;                  ," href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2456">62</a>]. Then the insertion time of LTR retrotransposons was dated according to the method described by JessyLabb [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Labbe J, Murat C, Morin E, Tuskan GA, Le Tacon F, Martin F: Characterization of transposable elements in the ectomycorrhizal fungus Laccaria bicolor. PLoS One. 2012, 7: e40197-" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2459">63</a>] (Supplementary Note and Figure S8 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec25">Evolution analysis</h3><p>Gene clustering was conducted with OrthoMCL [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Li L, Stoeckert CJ, Roos DS: OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 2003, 13: 2178-2189." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2473">64</a>] by setting the main inflation value to 1.5 and other parameters as default. PHYML [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Guindon S, Dufayard JF, Lefort V, Anisimova M, Hordijk W, Gascuel O: New algorithms and methods to estimate maximum-likelihood phylogenies: assessing the performance of PhyML 3.0. Syst Biol. 2010, 59: 307-321." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2476">65</a>] was selected to reconstruct the phylogenetic tree based on the HKY85 model [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Hasegawa M, Kishino H, Yano T: Dating of the human-ape splitting by a molecular clock of mitochondrial DNA. J Mol Evol. 1985, 22: 160-174." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2479">66</a>]. The program MCMCTree of the PAML package [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Yang Z: PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol Biol Evol. 2007, 24: 1586-1591." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2482">67</a>] was used to estimate species divergence time. Mcscan [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="MCscan. &#xA;                    http://chibba.agtec.uga.edu/duplication/mcscan&#xA;                    &#xA;                  ," href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2485">68</a>] was used to construct chromosome collinearity. Detailed descriptions about the identification of recent WGD events and two subgenomes are provided in Supplementary Note 4 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec26">Analysis of resistance genes in sesame</h3><p>HMMER V3.0 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Finn RD, Clements J, Eddy SR: HMMER web server: interactive sequence similarity searching. Nucleic Acids Res. 2011, Web Server Issue39: W29-W37." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2500">69</a>] was used to screen the predicted sesame proteome against the raw hidden Markov model corresponding to the Pfam NBS (NB-ARC), and further build a sesame-specific NBS hidden Markov model for screening. The TIR and LRR domains were identified using local Pfam_Scan (-E 0.01 --domE 0.01). MARCOIL [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Delorenzi M, Speed T: An HMM model for coiled-coil domains and a comparison with PSSM-based predictions. Bioinformatics. 2002, 18: 617-625." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2503">70</a>] with a threshold probability of 90 and the program paircoil2 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="McDonnell AV, Jiang T, Keating AE, Berger B: Paircoil2: improved prediction of coiled coils from sequence. Bioinformatics. 2006, 22: 356-358." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2506">71</a>] with a P-score cutoff of 0.025 were used as the settings for the CC motif identification.</p><p>The absence of NBS genes with a TIR domain in the sesame genome was further validated by checking the gene-masked assembly and the unassembled reads. For the masked assembly, we found nine NB-ARC fragments (&gt;300 bp), but no TIR hit was obtained. Among all the unmapped reads, only 19 showed homology to the TIR domain, but all the reads together covered less than half of the TIR region. Considering the above results, NBS genes with a TIR domain were absent from sesame (for detailed methods see Supplementary Note 5 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec27">Analysis of important characteristics in the genome</h3><p>The homologous lipid genes in sesame and other crops were identified by blastp (1e-5, identity &gt;30%) based on the database of acyl-Lipid metabolism in <i>A. thaliana</i>[<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Arabidopsis Acyl-lipid Metabolism. &#xA;                    http://aralip.plantbiology.msu.edu&#xA;                    &#xA;                  ," href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2526">72</a>] (for detailed methods see Supplementary Note 7 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec28">Genome resequencing and SNP calling</h3><p>For each accession, a paired-end sequencing library with insert sizes of 500 bp was constructed and then sequenced on the Hiseq 2000 platform. The raw reads were then subjected to a series of stringent filtering steps that had been used in <i>de novo</i> genome assembly (Supplementary Note 1.3 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>). Finally, we generated a total of more than 120 Gb clean data with each sample at over 13-fold sequence depth (Data S11 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM2">2</a>). The clean reads were mapped to the assembled sesame genome using BWA software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Li H, Durbin R: Fast and accurate short read alignment with Burrows-Wheeler transform. Bioinformatics. 2009, 25: 1754-1760." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2549">73</a>]. After mapping, SNPs were identified with read mapping quality 20 on the basis of the mpileup files generated by SAMtools [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Li H, Handsaker B, Wysoker A, Fennell T, Ruan J, Homer N, Marth G, Abecasis G, Durbin R: The Sequence Alignment/Map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics. 20782079, 2009: 25-" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2552">74</a>] (Data S7 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM2">2</a>). The SNPs extracted by the above process were first filtered by the sequencing depth: 30 and 581 using the vcfutils program in SAMtools. Then the raw SNP sites were further filtered using the following criteria: copy number 2 and a minimum of 5 bp apart with the exception of minor allele frequencies (0.05), whereby SNPs were retained when the distance between SNPs was less than 5 bp. Diversity parameters <i></i> and <i></i><sub>
                    <i>w</i>
                  </sub> were measured using a window of 10 kb with a step of 1 kb [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Xu X, Liu X, Ge S, Jensen JD, Hu F, Li X, Dong Y, Gutenkunst RN, Fang L, Huang L, Li J, He W, Zhang G, Zheng X, Zhang F, Li Y, Yu C, Kristiansen K, Zhang X, Wang J, Wright M, McCouch S, Nielsen R, Wang J, Wang W: Resequencing 50 accessions of cultivated and wild rice yields markers for identifying agronomically important genes. Nat Biotechnol. 2012, 30: 105-111." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2570">43</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Guo S, Zhang J, Sun H, Salse J, Lucas WJ, Zhang H, Zheng Y, Mao L, Ren Y, Wang Z, Min J, Guo X, Murat F, Ham BK, Zhang Z, Gao S, Huang M, Xu Y, Zhong S, Bombarely A, Mueller LA, Zhao H, He H, Zhang Y, Zhang Z, Huang S, Tan T, Pang E, Lin K, Hu Q, et al: The draft genome of watermelon (Citrullus lanatus) and resequencing of 20 diverse accessions. Nat Genet. 2012, 45: 51-58." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2573">45</a>].</p><p>Detection of copy number variations was performed as described by Zheng <i>et al.</i>[<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Zheng LY, Guo XS, He B, Sun LJ, Peng Y, Dong SS, Liu TF, Jiang S, Ramachandran S, Liu CM, Jing HC: Genome-wide patterns of genetic variation in sweet and grain sorghum (Sorghum bicolor). Genome Biol. 2011, 12: R114-" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2582">75</a>] and Jiao <i>et al</i>. [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Jiao Y, Zhao H, Ren L, Song W, Zeng B, Guo J, Wang B, Liu Z, Chen J, Li W, Zhang M, Xie S, Lai J: Genome-wide genetic changes during modern breeding of maize. Nat Genet. 2012, 44: 812-815." href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2588">76</a>] (Supplementary Note 8 in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#MOESM1">1</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec29">Data access</h3><p>Genomic data generated by the whole project are available at NCBI under accession number APMJ00000000 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Whole Genome Shotgun Sequencing Project of Sesamum indicum. &#xA;                    http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/APMJ00000000&#xA;                    &#xA;                  ," href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2603">77</a>]. WGS raw reads are deposited under the SRA study: SRA122008 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="The Sequence Read Archive (SRA) of the Genome of Sesamum indicum. &#xA;                    http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra/?term=SRA122008&#xA;                    &#xA;                  ," href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2606">78</a>]. The raw RNA-Seq data are deposited under the SRA study: SRA122023 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="The Sequence Read Archive (SRA) of the Transcriptomes of Sesamum indicum. &#xA;                    http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra/?term=SRA122023&#xA;                    &#xA;                  ," href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2609">79</a>]. Genome assembly, annotation and RNA-Seq data are also available at [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Sinbase: A Comprehensive Sesamum indicum Genomics Database. &#xA;                    http://ocri-genomics.org/Sinbase&#xA;                    &#xA;                  ," href="/articles/10.1186/gb-2014-15-2-r39#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d33850e2612">80</a>].</p></div></div></section>
                    <section aria-labelledby="abbreviations" data-title="Abbreviations"><div class="c-article-section" id="abbreviations-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="abbreviations">Abbreviations</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="abbreviations-content"><dl class="c-abbreviation_list"><dt class="c-abbreviation_list__term"><dfn>DPA:</dfn></dt><dd class="c-abbreviation_list__description">

LHW, SY, CS, RKV and CBT participated in the genome analysis and wrote the manuscript. YZZ, YL and WH participated in the study design and constructed the genetic map. LHW, SY, SYL and RKV participated in co-ordination and finalization of the manuscript. CS, XDZ, YW, DL, FL and CYX participated in the genome and transcriptome analyses. XLH and SST participated in the resequencing and analysis. YXZ and DHL prepared materials and performed the experiments. JYY performed the database construction. JYW, XX, YRL and SMH participated in the statistical analysis. All authors read and approved the final manuscript.</p><p>Linhai Wang, Sheng Yu, Chaobo Tong, Yingzhong Zhao, Yan Liu contributed equally to this work.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec30" data-title="Electronic supplementary material"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec30-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec30">Electronic supplementary material</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec30-content"><div data-test="supplementary-info"><div id="figshareContainer" class="c-article-figshare-container" data-test="figshare-container"></div>
